It automatically advances\n    82→ * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n    96→ * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n    97→ * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n    98→ * <p>\n    99→ * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n   100→ * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Migration Analysis\\n\\nThe analysis reveals a modern Kafka consumer architecture where the old ConsumerConnector API has been completely replaced. The current codebase contains two primary consumer implementations accessible through a delegation pattern.\\n\\n### New KafkaConsumer API Architecture (apache/kafka)\\n\\nThe **Consumer interface** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java) defines the contract for all consumer implementations. **KafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java) is the primary public implementation that delegates to either **ClassicKafkaConsumer** or **AsyncKafkaConsumer** based on configuration, using the **ConsumerDelegateCreator** pattern.\\n\\n**ClassicKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) provides backward compatibility with the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848). This is the synchronous consumer implementation where all network I/O happens in the application thread. It implements the **ConsumerDelegate** interface, which extends Consumer to expose internal methods for testing.\\n\\n**AsyncKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) represents the new asynchronous consumer using the newer group protocol (post-KIP 848).\\n\\n### Offset Management in New API\\n\\nOffset management in the new KafkaConsumer API uses the **OffsetAndMetadata** class (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java), which encapsulates the offset position along with optional metadata and leader epoch information. This represents a significant evolution from the old ConsumerConnector approach.\\n\\nThe **CommitRequestManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) handles offset commit operations. Key behavioral differences from the legacy API include:\\n1. Support for leader epochs to detect log truncation\\n2. Asynchronous and synchronous commit callbacks with guaranteed ordering\\n3. OffsetAndMetadata objects containing rich metadata including leader epoch\\n4. Automatic commit configuration via ConsumerConfig properties\\n\\nThe **OffsetFetcher** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java) manages offset validation and reset operations, including automatic offset reset strategies and leader epoch validation.\\n\\nThe **SubscriptionState** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) class tracks topic subscriptions, partition assignments, and consumer positions for all assigned partitions, maintaining thread-safe state management.\\n\\n### Camel Kafka Component Integration\\n\\nApache Camel integrates with the new KafkaConsumer API through its **KafkaConsumer** component (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), which is a Camel-specific consumer endpoint, not the Kafka consumer itself.\\n\\nCamel's offset management is abstracted through the **AbstractCommitManager** interface (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java), which provides multiple implementations:\\n- **SyncCommitManager** for synchronous offset commits using KafkaConsumer.commitSync()\\n- **AsyncCommitManager** for asynchronous offset commits\\n- **CommitManagers factory** (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManagers.java) for creating appropriate managers\\n\\nCamel's AbstractCommitManager.forceCommit() method wraps KafkaConsumer.commitSync() with OffsetAndMetadata, showing the migration pattern where offset+1 is committed to represent the next record to consume.\\n\\n### Key Behavioral Differences\\n\\n1. **Offset Representation**: The new API uses OffsetAndMetadata objects instead of simple long offsets, including leader epoch tracking for truncation detection\\n2. **Commit Callbacks**: The new API provides OffsetCommitCallback with guaranteed ordering of async commits before subsequent sync operations\\n3. **Auto-Commit**: Configured through ConsumerConfig.ENABLE_AUTO_COMMIT_CONFIG and AUTO_COMMIT_INTERVAL_MS_CONFIG properties\\n4. **Position Tracking**: Uses FetchPosition with OffsetAndMetadata in SubscriptionState for thread-safe tracking\\n5. **Backward Compatibility**: ClassicKafkaConsumer maintains compatibility with classic group protocol while AsyncKafkaConsumer uses the newer protocol\\n6. **Leader Epoch Support**: New API tracks leader epochs for robustness against log truncation scenarios\\n\\nThe migration from the old ConsumerConnector API to KafkaConsumer represents a shift from complex, protocol-specific implementations to a more unified, feature-rich consumer API with better offset management, truncation detection, and group protocol flexibility.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2722,"cache_read_input_tokens":65841,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2722},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"de91ea77-6b05-45eb-9c06-b21034cf03cf","uuid":"05cc9ac3-6392-4931-a35c-53832c82f2c7"}

Migration Analysis\\n\\nThe analysis reveals a modern Kafka consumer architecture where the old ConsumerConnector API has been completely replaced. The current codebase contains two primary consumer implementations accessible through a delegation pattern.\\n\\n### New KafkaConsumer API Architecture (apache/kafka)\\n\\nThe **Consumer interface** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java) defines the contract for all consumer implementations. **KafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java) is the primary public implementation that delegates to either **ClassicKafkaConsumer** or **AsyncKafkaConsumer** based on configuration, using the **ConsumerDelegateCreator** pattern.\\n\\n**ClassicKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) provides backward compatibility with the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848). This is the synchronous consumer implementation where all network I/O happens in the application thread. It implements the **ConsumerDelegate** interface, which extends Consumer to expose internal methods for testing.\\n\\n**AsyncKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) represents the new asynchronous consumer using the newer group protocol (post-KIP 848).\\n\\n### Offset Management in New API\\n\\nOffset management in the new KafkaConsumer API uses the **OffsetAndMetadata** class (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java), which encapsulates the offset position along with optional metadata and leader epoch information. This represents a significant evolution from the old ConsumerConnector approach.\\n\\nThe **CommitRequestManager** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) handles offset commit operations. Key behavioral differences from the legacy API include:\\n1. Support for leader epochs to detect log truncation\\n2. Asynchronous and synchronous commit callbacks with guaranteed ordering\\n3. OffsetAndMetadata objects containing rich metadata including leader epoch\\n4. Automatic commit configuration via ConsumerConfig properties\\n\\nThe **OffsetFetcher** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java) manages offset validation and reset operations, including automatic offset reset strategies and leader epoch validation.\\n\\nThe **SubscriptionState** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) class tracks topic subscriptions, partition assignments, and consumer positions for all assigned partitions, maintaining thread-safe state management.\\n\\n### Camel Kafka Component Integration\\n\\nApache Camel integrates with the new KafkaConsumer API through its **KafkaConsumer** component (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), which is a Camel-specific consumer endpoint, not the Kafka consumer itself.\\n\\nCamel's offset management is abstracted through the **AbstractCommitManager** interface (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/AbstractCommitManager.java), which provides multiple implementations:\\n- **SyncCommitManager** for synchronous offset commits using KafkaConsumer.commitSync()\\n- **AsyncCommitManager** for asynchronous offset commits\\n- **CommitManagers factory** (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/consumer/CommitManagers.java) for creating appropriate managers\\n\\nCamel's AbstractCommitManager.forceCommit() method wraps KafkaConsumer.commitSync() with OffsetAndMetadata, showing the migration pattern where offset+1 is committed to represent the next record to consume.\\n\\n### Key Behavioral Differences\\n\\n1. **Offset Representation**: The new API uses OffsetAndMetadata objects instead of simple long offsets, including leader epoch tracking for truncation detection\\n2. **Commit Callbacks**: The new API provides OffsetCommitCallback with guaranteed ordering of async commits before subsequent sync operations\\n3. **Auto-Commit**: Configured through ConsumerConfig.ENABLE_AUTO_COMMIT_CONFIG and AUTO_COMMIT_INTERVAL_MS_CONFIG properties\\n4. **Position Tracking**: Uses FetchPosition with OffsetAndMetadata in SubscriptionState for thread-safe tracking\\n5. **Backward Compatibility**: ClassicKafkaConsumer maintains compatibility with classic group protocol while AsyncKafkaConsumer uses the newer protocol\\n6. **Leader Epoch Support**: New API tracks leader epochs for robustness against log truncation scenarios\\n\\nThe migration from the old ConsumerConnector API to KafkaConsumer represents a shift from complex, protocol-specific implementations to a more unified, feature-rich consumer API with better offset management, truncation detection, and group protocol flexibility.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
